## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time and population size, which is the canonical form of population dynamics ODEs. The relationship likely involves density-dependent feedback mechanisms where growth rate depends on current population P, possibly with time-varying parameters.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Allee effect (weak/cubic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 - c2 * P) (enhanced growth at intermediate densities)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic vs catabolic scaling)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * (c2 + 1)**(-1) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t) (carrying capacity changing with time)
- Exponential decay of growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent intrinsic growth rate)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with contest competition minus mortality)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (simplest polynomial density dependence)
- Hassell-type: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P)**c2 - c3 * P (generalized competition model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent negative feedback → multiplicative factor (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)**n) representing carrying capacity limitation
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) → additional multiplicative factor (P - c) or (1 + c*P) creating a hump-shaped per-capita growth rate
- Per-capita growth rate declining linearly with P → dP/dt is quadratic in P (logistic signature: c0*P + c1*P²)
- Metabolic scaling in growth → difference of power laws: c0*P^a - c1*P^b where a < b (anabolism vs catabolism)
- Logarithmic self-limitation → log(c/P) or log(P) terms indicating Gompertz-type multiplicative degradation of growth rate
- Seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing → sin(c0*t) or cos(c0*t) multiplicative modulation of growth parameters
- Cooperative/competitive switching → ratio P/(c+P) indicating transition from cooperation-dominated to competition-dominated regimes
- Immigration/emigration constant flux → additive constant term c0 independent of P representing external population input/output

## Analysis

The Ground Truth expression is:
$$GT = 0.9540 \cdot (1 - P/96.907) \cdot P + 0.9540 \cdot P^{1/3}$$

Expanding:
$$GT = 0.9540 \cdot P - 0.009845 \cdot P^2 + 0.9540 \cdot P^{1/3}$$

This is equivalent to:
$$GT = c_a \cdot P^{1/3} + c_b \cdot P^2 + c_c \cdot P$$

where $c_a = 0.9540$, $c_b = -0.009845$, $c_c = 0.9540$.

Now I need to find candidates that can reduce to $P^{1/3} \cdot c_0 + P^2 \cdot c_1 + P \cdot c_2$ with no dependence on $t$ and no extra terms.

**Candidate 62**: $P^{1/3} c_0 + P^2 c_1 + P c_2$

This is an exact structural match! Setting:
- $c_0 = 0.9540$
- $c_1 = -0.009845$
- $c_2 = 0.9540$

gives exactly the GT.

Many other candidates also match (e.g., candidates 60, 71, 73, 74, etc., which include additional terms that can be zeroed out), but **Candidate 62** is the simplest exact match.
